<p><b>Rio Gavin Ferdinand</b> (born 7 November 1978) is an English former professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who played as a <a href="/wiki/Defender_(association_football)#Centre-back" title="Defender (association football)">centre-back</a>. He played 81 times for the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England national football team</a> between 1997 and 2011, and was a member of three <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> squads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> He is regarded by many to be one of England's greatest ever players and he is one of the most decorated English footballers of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ferdinand began his football career playing for various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Youth_team" title="Youth team">youth teams</a>, finally settling at <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a> where he progressed through the youth ranks and made his professional Premier League debut in 1996. He became a fan favourite, winning the 'Hammer of the Year award' the following season. He earned his first senior international cap in a match against <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">Cameroon</a> in 1997, setting a record as the youngest defender to play for England at the time. His achievements and footballing potential attracted <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a> and he transferred to the club for a record-breaking fee of <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>18 million. He spent two seasons at the club, becoming the <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">team captain</a> in 2001.</p>
<p>He joined <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchester_United" title="Manchester United">Manchester United</a> in July 2002 <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_association_football_transfers" title="List of most expensive association football transfers">for around £30 million, breaking the transfer fee record</a> once more. He won the Premier League, his first major club honour, in a successful first season at the club. In September 2003, he missed a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drugs_test" title="Drugs test">drugs test</a> and was banned from competition for eight months from January until September 2004, causing him to miss half a Premier League season, Manchester United's FA Cup triumph, and the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2004" title="UEFA Euro 2004">Euro 2004</a> international competition. Upon his return, he established himself in the Manchester United first team and received plaudits for his performances, featuring in the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year" title="PFA Team of the Year">PFA Team of the Year</a> four times in five years. More club success followed with another Premier League win in the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_FA_Premier_League" title="2006–07 FA Premier League">2006–07 season</a> and a Premier League and <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> double the following year. His career at United, in which he won 6 Premier League titles and over 15 trophies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> ended when his contract expired in 2014, and he subsequently joined <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a> where he played for just one season before being released from the club as a result of their relegation from the Premier League. He announced his retirement from professional football on 30 May 2015.</p>
<p>His brother, <a href="/wiki/Anton_Ferdinand" title="Anton Ferdinand">Anton</a>, also a centre-back, plays for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southend_United" title="Southend United">Southend United</a>, former England international striker <a href="/wiki/Les_Ferdinand" title="Les Ferdinand">Les Ferdinand</a> and former <a href="/wiki/Dagenham_%26_Redbridge_F.C." title="Dagenham &amp; Redbridge F.C.">Dagenham &amp; Redbridge</a> midfielder <a href="/wiki/Kane_Ferdinand" title="Kane Ferdinand">Kane Ferdinand</a> are his cousins.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formative_years_and_education">Formative years and education</span></h3>
<p>Ferdinand was born at <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College_Hospital" title="King's College Hospital">King's College Hospital</a> in <a href="/wiki/Camberwell" title="Camberwell">Camberwell</a>, but grew up in <a href="/wiki/Peckham" title="Peckham">Peckham</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> He is the son of an Irish mother, Janice Lavender, and a <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucian</a> father, Julian Ferdinand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StLucia_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-StLucia-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ferdinand grew up in Peckham in a large family. <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Both parents worked to support the family, his mother as a child carer and his father as a tailor. His parents never married and they separated when he was 14 years old. His father remained close, moving to a nearby estate, and took the kids to football training and to local parks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caspar_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Caspar-12">[12]</a></sup> Ferdinand attended Camelot Primary School.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caspar_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Caspar-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jones_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jones-13">[13]</a></sup> At school, he focused on maths and revelled in the opportunity to perform before an audience during a school production of <i><a href="/wiki/Bugsy_Malone" title="Bugsy Malone">Bugsy Malone</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caspar_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-Caspar-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>"I always as a kid wanted to do something different, I'd get bored very easily – even playing football or hanging around with my mates. So travelling away from home, meeting new people. ... I enjoyed it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caspar_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-Caspar-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>He chose to attend <a href="/wiki/Blackheath_Bluecoat_Church_of_England_School" title="Blackheath Bluecoat Church of England School">Blackheath Bluecoat School</a> to make new friends and settled in well, feeling his confidence growing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-10">[10]</a></sup> His second year was marred by the death of a fellow pupil, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stephen_Lawrence" title="Stephen Lawrence">Stephen Lawrence</a>, and the event demonstrated the ever-present threat of violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jones_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jones-13">[13]</a></sup> Ferdinand enjoyed physical expression, taking part in not just football and gymnastics classes but drama, theatre and ballet too.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caspar_12-4"><a href="#cite_note-Caspar-12">[12]</a></sup> He was an able child: he represented <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Southwark" title="London Borough of Southwark">Southwark</a> in gymnastics at the <a href="/wiki/London_Youth_Games" title="London Youth Games">London Youth Games</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> by age 10 he had been invited to train at the <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a> academy, and at age 11 he won a scholarship to attend the <a href="/wiki/Central_School_of_Ballet" title="Central School of Ballet">Central School of Ballet</a> in London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-10">[10]</a></sup> Ferdinand attended the ballet classes, travelling to the city centre four days a week for four years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caspar_12-5"><a href="#cite_note-Caspar-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth_team_career">Youth team career</span></h3>
<p>Ferdinand's superior footballing abilities were evident even as a child: when he was 11 years old a youth coach, David Goodwin, remarked "I'm going to call you Pelé, son, I like the way you play."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caspar_12-6"><a href="#cite_note-Caspar-12">[12]</a></sup> Ferdinand was regularly playing in youth teams and at Eltham Town he played as an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Attacking_midfielder" title="Attacking midfielder">attacking midfielder</a> but team scouts saw the young player had the physical potential to be a <a href="/wiki/Defender_(association_football)#Centre-back" title="Defender (association football)">centre-back</a> instead. Teams vied for the young footballer's services and during his youth he trained with <a href="/wiki/Charlton_Athletic_F.C." title="Charlton Athletic F.C.">Charlton Athletic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C" title="Chelsea F.C">Chelsea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Millwall_F.C." title="Millwall F.C.">Millwall</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers" title="Queens Park Rangers">Queens Park Rangers</a>. Ferdinand was ever curious of different places and even travelled north to <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a>'s training ground, spending a good part of his school holidays in a bedsit just to be there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caspar_12-7"><a href="#cite_note-Caspar-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>London team <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Ham_United" title="West Ham United">West Ham United</a> was to be his footballing home, however, and he joined their <a href="/wiki/Youth_system" title="Youth system">youth system</a> in 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_10-4"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-10">[10]</a></sup> He signed his first <a href="/wiki/Youth_Training_Scheme" title="Youth Training Scheme">Youth Training Scheme</a> contract in January 1994 and played alongside players such as <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lampard" title="Frank Lampard">Frank Lampard</a> at the academy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caspar_12-8"><a href="#cite_note-Caspar-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Success pending at club level, international football also began for Ferdinand; at 16 he joined the England youth team squad to compete in their age group's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Football_Championship" title="UEFA European Football Championship">UEFA European Football Championship</a>, gaining his first experience of international competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caspar_12-9"><a href="#cite_note-Caspar-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Senior_career">Senior career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="West_Ham_United">West Ham United</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anton_and_Rio_Ferdinand_with_West_Ham_United.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1757" data-file-width="1626" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Anton_and_Rio_Ferdinand_with_West_Ham_United.jpg/220px-Anton_and_Rio_Ferdinand_with_West_Ham_United.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Anton_and_Rio_Ferdinand_with_West_Ham_United.jpg/330px-Anton_and_Rio_Ferdinand_with_West_Ham_United.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Anton_and_Rio_Ferdinand_with_West_Ham_United.jpg/440px-Anton_and_Rio_Ferdinand_with_West_Ham_United.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Anton_and_Rio_Ferdinand_with_West_Ham_United.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rio and Anton Ferdinand playing in <a href="/wiki/Tony_Carr" title="Tony Carr">Tony Carr</a>'s testimonial match in 2010.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Originally scouted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frank_Lampard_Sr." title="Frank Lampard Sr.">Frank Lampard</a>, Ferdinand progressed through the youth team ranks, earning a professional contract and a place in the first team squad in the process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caspar_12-10"><a href="#cite_note-Caspar-12">[12]</a></sup> On 5 May 1996, he made his senior team debut, as he came on as a substitute for <a href="/wiki/Tony_Cottee" title="Tony Cottee">Tony Cottee</a> in the Hammers' last game of the season, a 1–1 home draw against <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C." title="Sheffield Wednesday F.C.">Sheffield Wednesday</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caspar_12-11"><a href="#cite_note-Caspar-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> During the summer of 1997, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> made enquires about Ferdinand before they turned to <a href="/wiki/Henning_Berg" title="Henning Berg">Henning Berg</a> after West Ham rejected any sale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 1997–98 season, Ferdinand won the Hammer of the Year award at the young age of 19.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GUIDE_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-GUIDE-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bournemouth">Bournemouth</span></h3>
<p>In November 1996 Ferdinand joined <a href="/wiki/A.F.C._Bournemouth" title="A.F.C. Bournemouth">Bournemouth</a> on loan. He made his debut on 9 November in a 1–1 away draw against <a href="/wiki/Blackpool_F.C." title="Blackpool F.C.">Blackpool</a>. He played 10 games for Bournemouth before returning to West Ham in January 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leeds_United">Leeds United</span></h3>
<p>Ferdinand joined <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FA_Premier_League" title="FA Premier League">Premier League</a> club <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a> in November 2000 for <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>18 million, then a British transfer record as well as becoming the world's most expensive defender.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GUIDE_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-GUIDE-18">[18]</a></sup> Despite an uncomfortable start to his career at <a href="/wiki/Elland_Road" title="Elland Road">Elland Road</a>, beginning with a 3–1 defeat at <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester CIty</a> on his debut,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Ferdinand settled well and became an integral part of the Leeds team that reached the semi-final stage of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>, scoring with a header in the quarter-final against Spain's <a href="/wiki/Deportivo_de_La_Coru%C3%B1a" title="Deportivo de La Coruña">Deportivo La Coruña</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Other highlights during his spell in Yorkshire included goals against <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> at <a href="/wiki/Anfield" title="Anfield">Anfield</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> and a scoring return to Upton Park.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>The following season, in August 2001, he became the club <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">captain</a> after replacing <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Radebe" title="Lucas Radebe">Lucas Radebe</a> and turned in an impressive second campaign, despite Leeds' failure to break into the top four and secure qualification for the competition they had figured in so prominently during the previous season. During the <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002 FIFA World Cup</a>, rumours began circulating that the club were in dire financial trouble and that new manager <a href="/wiki/Terry_Venables" title="Terry Venables">Terry Venables</a> would be forced to part with his star defender for a substantial amount of cash. Later that summer after Ferdinand's impressive World Cup for England, Leeds accepted a bid of £29.1 million due to their perilous financial position.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manchester_United">Manchester United</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2002.E2.80.932007">2002–2007</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:R_Ferdinand.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="301" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/R_Ferdinand.jpg/170px-R_Ferdinand.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/R_Ferdinand.jpg/255px-R_Ferdinand.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0d/R_Ferdinand.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:R_Ferdinand.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ferdinand for Manchester United in 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 22 July 2002, Ferdinand joined fellow Premier League side Manchester United on a five-year deal to become the most expensive British footballer in history at the time and the world's most expensive defender for a second time, a title he had lost in 2001 to <a href="/wiki/Lilian_Thuram" title="Lilian Thuram">Lilian Thuram</a>. The fee included a basic element in the high £20 millions, and some conditional elements, which allowed Leeds to tell their fans that they were selling him for over £30 million. <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a> later took a single payment in place of all the contingent elements during their financial crisis. The final book value of Ferdinand's contract in Manchester United's accounts was £34 million. This included agents' fees, with Leeds receiving just under £30 million. Ferdinand went on to win the Premier League title with Manchester United in his first season at the club. He collected a winner's medal in the <a href="/wiki/2006_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2006 Football League Cup Final">2006 League Cup</a>, with runners-up medals in the <a href="/wiki/2003_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2003 Football League Cup Final">2003 League Cup</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2005_FA_Cup_Final" title="2005 FA Cup Final">2005 FA Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2003, he failed to attend a <a href="/wiki/Drug_test" title="Drug test">drug test</a> scheduled to take place at United's Carrington training ground. Ferdinand had left after training to go shopping, only to remember and attempt to return, only to be told it was too late. He did undergo testing the following day and passed, and also offered to have a hair follicle test, which would provide results for the previous six months, but the FA turned down the offer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">The FA Disciplinary Committee</a> chaired by <a href="/wiki/Barry_Bright" title="Barry Bright">Barry Bright</a> imposed an eight-month ban from January 2004 at club and international level and a £50,000 fine, meaning he would miss the rest of the season and some of the next along with all of <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2004" title="UEFA Euro 2004">Euro 2004</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Manchester United appealed against the verdict and sought to draw parallels to the case of <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> player <a href="/wiki/Christian_Negouai" title="Christian Negouai">Christian Negouai</a>, who was fined £2,000 for missing a test. However, <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> president <a href="/wiki/Sepp_Blatter" title="Sepp Blatter">Sepp Blatter</a> stated that such comparisons are inappropriate due to differences between the two cases. Negouai had been stuck in traffic and was willing to take the test, while Ferdinand was charged with "failure or refusal" to attend the test. Both the FA and FIFA sought to have the ban increased to 12 months (half the possible maximum). In the end, the original verdict was upheld.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 December 2005, in a game against <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Athletic_F.C." title="Wigan Athletic F.C.">Wigan Athletic</a>, Ferdinand scored his first goal for United, en route to a 4–0 victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> This was his first goal after more than three years at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a>. He followed this up with a powerfully headed goal against <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> He then scored a last minute winner against <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> at Old Trafford,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> possibly his most important Manchester United goal to date. In the corresponding fixture in the following season on 22 October 2006, Ferdinand scored again in a 2–0 victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following impressive and consistent performances in the league, Rio Ferdinand was named in the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_in_English_football" title="2006–07 in English football">2006–07</a> <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year" title="PFA Team of the Year">PFA Premiership Team of the Season</a>, alongside seven of his Manchester United team-mates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2007.E2.80.932014">2007–2014</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rio_Juventus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1962" data-file-width="2190" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Rio_Juventus.jpg/220px-Rio_Juventus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Rio_Juventus.jpg/330px-Rio_Juventus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Rio_Juventus.jpg/440px-Rio_Juventus.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rio_Juventus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ferdinand with <a href="/wiki/Olof_Mellberg" title="Olof Mellberg">Olof Mellberg</a> in a match against <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> in 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ferdinand started the 2007–08 season well, he was part of a United defence that managed to keep six clean sheets in a row in the Premier League, before conceding an early goal to <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Villa_Park_(stadium)" title="Villa Park (stadium)">Villa Park</a> on 20 October 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> It was also during this game where Ferdinand scored his first goal of the season, which was United's third goal of that game, with a left foot strike which took a very strong deflection off one of Villa's defenders. Just three days later, Ferdinand scored his first European goal for United by opening the scoring against <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Kyiv" title="FC Dynamo Kyiv">Dynamo Kyiv</a>, with a superb header. United dominated the game and won 4–2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 12 January 2008, Ferdinand bagged a rare Premier League goal in a 6–0 hammering of <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a> at Old Trafford. In their FA Cup quarter-final match against <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a> on 8 March 2008 when <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> dominated, Ferdinand made a rare appearance as a goalkeeper, after <a href="/wiki/Edwin_van_der_Sar" title="Edwin van der Sar">Edwin van der Sar</a> left the pitch with a groin injury and the replacement keeper, <a href="/wiki/Tomasz_Kuszczak" title="Tomasz Kuszczak">Tomasz Kuszczak</a>, was sent off after conceding a penalty. Despite diving the right way, he was unable to save <a href="/wiki/Sulley_Muntari" title="Sulley Muntari">Sulley Muntari</a>'s spot kick, and Manchester United were eliminated from the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> On 6 April 2008, against <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a>, Ferdinand limped out of the match due to a foot injury. He was rated doubtful whether he would face <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">A.S. Roma</a> in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> quarter-final second leg on 9 April 2008. He would play the full 90 minutes, though he received three stitches at half-time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>After United's 2–1 loss to Chelsea in the Premier League in April 2008, Ferdinand swore at Chelsea stewards and tried to kick a wall in the tunnel, but instead kicked a female steward, Tracy Wray. Ferdinand claimed to have merely brushed her with his foot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> He said he had apologised and sent the steward some flowers. However, Wray showed the bruise on her leg to the media, and her husband claimed that Ferdinand had not apologised or sent flowers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ferdinand_Fabregas.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2407" data-file-width="1799" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Ferdinand_Fabregas.jpg/170px-Ferdinand_Fabregas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Ferdinand_Fabregas.jpg/255px-Ferdinand_Fabregas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Ferdinand_Fabregas.jpg/340px-Ferdinand_Fabregas.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ferdinand_Fabregas.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ferdinand as <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">captain</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2008–09 UEFA Champions League">2008–09 Champions League</a> semi-final.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>It was announced on 16 April 2008 that, along with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Carrick" title="Michael Carrick">Michael Carrick</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wes_Brown" title="Wes Brown">Wes Brown</a>, Ferdinand had agreed to sign a new five-year contract, worth around £130,000 a week, which would keep him with United until 2013. The contract was finally signed on 15 May 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> On 21 May 2008, Ferdinand captained Manchester United to a <a href="/wiki/2008_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2008 UEFA Champions League Final">Champions League Final</a> victory versus <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> He accepted the trophy together with <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Giggs" title="Ryan Giggs">Ryan Giggs</a>, as Giggs was the on field captain for most of the matches during that season during <a href="/wiki/Gary_Neville" title="Gary Neville">Gary Neville</a>'s absence due to injury.</p>
<p>In an interview with <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_5_Live" title="BBC Radio 5 Live">BBC Radio 5 Live</a> he criticised FIFA's approach to tackling racism in football, stating that not enough was being done to punish those guilty of homophobic or racist abuse at matches. Regarding taunts aimed at <a href="/wiki/Emile_Heskey" title="Emile Heskey">Emile Heskey</a> in England's 4–1 victory against Croatia in <a href="/wiki/Zagreb" title="Zagreb">Zagreb</a>, Ferdinand remarked:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"Croatia were fined a few thousand quid. What's that going to do? That is not going to stop people shouting racist or homophobic abuse...If things like this keep happening you have to take points off them. Then the punters will realise the team is going to be punished."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Ferdinand had an injury plagued 2009–10 season, a number of back and knee injuries kept him on the sidelines for months. He returned to action on 28 January 2010, but was banned for four games after being found guilty of violent conduct for elbowing <a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Craig_Fagan" title="Craig Fagan">Craig Fagan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>Due to a knee injury he suffered in the summer of 2010, which ruled him out of the World Cup for England, he missed all of pre-season, the Community Shield and the first four games of the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Premier_League" title="2010–11 Premier League">2010–11 Premier League</a> season. He returned to first-team football in the opening game of the Champions League group stage against <a href="/wiki/Rangers_F.C." title="Rangers F.C.">Rangers</a> on 14 September. He captained the side and played the full 90 minutes in a goalless draw. He started the season opening game in August 2011, the <a href="/wiki/2011_FA_Community_Shield" title="2011 FA Community Shield">2011 FA Community Shield</a>, where United found themselves 2–0 down at half time to city rivals <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a>. Ferdinand was taken off after 45 minutes along with defensive partner <a href="/wiki/Nemanja_Vidi%C4%87" title="Nemanja Vidić">Nemanja Vidić</a> and replaced by <a href="/wiki/Jonny_Evans" title="Jonny Evans">Jonny Evans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phil_Jones_(footballer,_born_1992)" title="Phil Jones (footballer, born 1992)">Phil Jones</a> respectively. United went on to win the game 3–2 and Ferdinand claimed his fourth Community Shield medal of his career. Ferdinand started in the opening <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> match of the season at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion" title="West Bromwich Albion">West Bromwich Albion</a>, a game United won 2–1, but he went off with a hamstring injury after 75 minutes. After the match <a href="/wiki/Alex_Ferguson" title="Alex Ferguson">Alex Ferguson</a> confirmed that Ferdinand would be out for six weeks. Ferdinand however recovered much quicker than initially diagnosed and returned to take a place on the bench two weeks later at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a> in United's 8–2 demolition of <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a>, although he did not play a part in the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Ferdinand made his return to competitive action in a 1–1 draw against <a href="/wiki/Stoke_City_F.C." title="Stoke City F.C.">Stoke City</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Britannia_Stadium" title="Britannia Stadium">Britannia Stadium</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rio_Ferdinand_QPR.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1646" data-file-width="812" height="304" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Rio_Ferdinand_QPR.JPG/150px-Rio_Ferdinand_QPR.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Rio_Ferdinand_QPR.JPG/225px-Rio_Ferdinand_QPR.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Rio_Ferdinand_QPR.JPG/300px-Rio_Ferdinand_QPR.JPG 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rio_Ferdinand_QPR.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ferdinand with Queens Park Rangers, October 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 9 December 2012, Ferdinand was struck and injured by a coin thrown from the home crowd during United's 3–2 <a href="/wiki/Manchester_derby" title="Manchester derby">derby</a> victory away from home against Manchester City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 5 March 2013, Ferdinand, unhappy with the referee <a href="/wiki/C%C3%BCneyt_%C3%87ak%C4%B1r" title="Cüneyt Çakır">Cüneyt Çakır</a>'s decision to send off <a href="/wiki/Nani" title="Nani">Nani</a> during a 2–1 Champions League defeat to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Madrid" title="Real Madrid">Real Madrid</a> at Old Trafford, clapped sarcastically in the referee's face after the game. He escaped any punishment from UEFA for the incident.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 12 May 2013, Ferdinand scored the winner and final goal of the <a href="/wiki/Alex_Ferguson" title="Alex Ferguson">Sir Alex Ferguson</a> era at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a> in a 2–1 victory over <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swansea_City" title="Swansea City">Swansea City</a>. After a corner was missed by everyone, the ball found its way to Ferdinand at the back post and he hit it on the volley to seal the win. On 23 May 2013, it was announced that Ferdinand had secured a new one-year contract that would see him stay with the club until the end of the 2013–14 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> He was not offered an extension when that contract expired, and agreed to leave Manchester United on 12 May 2014. In a letter on his official website, he said "I am feeling fit and healthy, ready for a new challenge and looking forward to whatever the future holds for me."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Queens_Park_Rangers">Queens Park Rangers</span></h3>
<p>On 17 July 2014, Ferdinand signed for newly promoted Premier League club <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a> on a one-year contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> He returned to <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a> for the first time since leaving Manchester United on 14 September 2014 to face his former club in the Premier League in which his side was beaten 4–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2014, Ferdinand confirmed in an interview on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jonathan_Ross_Show" title="The Jonathan Ross Show">The Jonathan Ross Show</a></i> that he would retire at the end of the season, saying "I'm not fearful of retirement, I'm looking forward to it, I can see some good stuff hopefully happening ahead".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> In May 2015, following their relegation, Queens Park Rangers announced the release of Ferdinand in the summer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> He made only 12 appearances for QPR in his only season with the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 30 May 2015, Ferdinand announced his retirement from professional football, three days after leaving QPR.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:England_team.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1462" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/England_team.jpg/220px-England_team.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/England_team.jpg/330px-England_team.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/England_team.jpg/440px-England_team.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:England_team.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ferdinand <i>(wearing No.5)</i> lining up for <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> against <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_national_football_team" title="Paraguay national football team">Paraguay</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ferdinand was <a href="/wiki/Cap_(sport)" title="Cap (sport)">capped</a> 81 times<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> for England making him England's second <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team#Most_capped_players" title="England national football team">most capped</a> black player behind <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Cole" title="Ashley Cole">Ashley Cole</a> with 107.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Although Ferdinand was named in four consecutive England World Cup squads (albeit without playing in 1998 and missing 2010 through injury), he never went to a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Championship" title="UEFA European Championship">European Championship</a> due to a ban for missing a drugs test and due to England's failure to qualify for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008" title="UEFA Euro 2008">UEFA Euro 2008</a>.</p>
<p>Ferdinand scored three goals for England,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> the first in the <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup#Round_of_16" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002 World Cup second round</a> match against <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark</a> (although some sources credit this goal as a <a href="/wiki/Thomas_S%C3%B8rensen" title="Thomas Sørensen">Thomas Sørensen</a> <a href="/wiki/Own_goal" title="Own goal">own goal</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>). The second was a near post strike that beat the Russian goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Vyacheslav_Malafeev" title="Vyacheslav Malafeev">Vyacheslav Malafeev</a> in England's <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2008 qualifying">Euro 2008 qualifier</a> against <a href="/wiki/Russia_national_football_team" title="Russia national football team">Russia</a> on 12 September 2007 at Wembley Stadium. The third on 11 October 2008 in a <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a> qualifying match at home to <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan_national_football_team" title="Kazakhstan national football team">Kazakhstan</a>. England won 5–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the age of 19 years and 8 days, Ferdinand earned his first full <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> cap as a substitute in a friendly against <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">Cameroon</a> on 15 November 1997, making him the youngest defender to play for England at the time (a record broken in 2006 by <a href="/wiki/Micah_Richards" title="Micah Richards">Micah Richards</a>). Ferdinand would have made an even earlier debut in September had he not been charged with drink-driving in the buildup to England's <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="1998 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">1998 World Cup qualifier</a> against <a href="/wiki/Moldova_national_football_team" title="Moldova national football team">Moldova</a>. Ferdinand was named in the squad for this game and was a likely starter; however, the public mourning for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Princess_Diana" title="Princess Diana">Princess Diana</a> – whose chauffeur had been suspected of drink-driving – left <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Hoddle" title="Glenn Hoddle">Glenn Hoddle</a> with little choice but to drop the teenager from the squad.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> After an impressive <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_West_Ham_United_F.C._season" title="1997–98 West Ham United F.C. season">1997–98 season</a> he was selected for the <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">1998 World Cup</a> squad as a back-up defender. However, he was not selected in <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Keegan" title="Kevin Keegan">Kevin Keegan</a>'s 22-man squad for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2000" title="UEFA Euro 2000">the 2000 European Championships</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>After his £18 million move to Leeds United, Ferdinand was named in the starting line-up by <a href="/wiki/Caretaker_manager" title="Caretaker manager">caretaker manager</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peter_Taylor_(footballer_born_1953)" title="Peter Taylor (footballer born 1953)">Peter Taylor</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Exhibition_game" title="Exhibition game">friendly match</a> against <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> and quickly established himself as a first-choice player under <a href="/wiki/Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson" title="Sven-Göran Eriksson">Sven-Göran Eriksson</a>. He was selected as one of England's two first-choice centre-backs at the <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002</a> and <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006</a> <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cups</a>, wearing the number 5 shirt.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/John_Terry" title="John Terry">John Terry</a> (with whom Ferdinand would later partner in central defence) replaced Ferdinand in the England side throughout his eight-month ban until his return on 9 October 2004 in their <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="2006 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">World Cup qualifier</a> against <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_football_team" title="Wales national football team">Wales</a>. Ferdinand played ten <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup finals</a> matches for England, recording clean sheets against <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_national_football_team" title="Nigeria national football team">Nigeria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark</a> in 2002, and <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_national_football_team" title="Paraguay national football team">Paraguay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_national_football_team" title="Trinidad and Tobago national football team">Trinidad &amp; Tobago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador_national_football_team" title="Ecuador national football team">Ecuador</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a> in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rio_Ferdinand-en.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="465" data-file-width="508" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Rio_Ferdinand-en.JPG/220px-Rio_Ferdinand-en.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Rio_Ferdinand-en.JPG/330px-Rio_Ferdinand-en.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Rio_Ferdinand-en.JPG/440px-Rio_Ferdinand-en.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rio_Ferdinand-en.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ferdinand on international duty, 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 25 March 2008 it was announced that Ferdinand would wear the <a href="/wiki/Captain_(sports)" title="Captain (sports)">captain's armband</a> for <a href="/wiki/Fabio_Capello" title="Fabio Capello">Fabio Capello</a>'s second game in charge of the national team,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> ahead of <a href="/wiki/John_Terry" title="John Terry">John Terry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steven_Gerrard" title="Steven Gerrard">Steven Gerrard</a> or <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a>, who some believed would be named captain to mark his 100th cap for his country. An <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">FA</a> statement suggested that the decision to name Ferdinand as captain was part of Capello's plans of rotating the captaincy before naming an official captain for September's <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="2010 FIFA World Cup qualification">World Cup qualifiers</a>. On 19 August, however, Ferdinand lost out to Terry in retaining the captain's armband but was named vice-captain by Fabio Capello.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>A mistake in the match between England and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine_national_football_team" title="Ukraine national football team">Ukraine</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dnipropetrovsk" title="Dnipropetrovsk">Dnipropetrovsk</a> on 10 October 2009 which led to the <a href="/wiki/Ejection_(sports)" title="Ejection (sports)">sending off</a> of <a href="/wiki/Robert_Green" title="Robert Green">Robert Green</a> led some to question his inclusion in the squad. A lack of match practice for his club and a series of errors such as he suffered in his early days as a footballer led to criticism of his inclusion from several corners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 5 February 2010, Ferdinand replaced <a href="/wiki/John_Terry" title="John Terry">John Terry</a> as captain of England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although back and groin injury problems forced him to miss much of the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Manchester_United_F.C._season" title="2009–10 Manchester United F.C. season">2009–10 domestic season</a>, Ferdinand was selected to captain England at the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 World Cup</a>. However, he suffered a knee ligament injury during the team's first training session in South Africa on 4 June and was subsequently ruled out of the tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> On 19 March 2011, ahead of England's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012_qualification" title="UEFA Euro 2012 qualification">Euro 2012 qualifier</a> against <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_football_team" title="Wales national football team">Wales</a>, Capello announced that John Terry was to be re-instated as permanent England captain and that Ferdinand would return to his role of vice-captain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ferdinand was left out of <a href="/wiki/Roy_Hodgson" title="Roy Hodgson">Roy Hodgson</a>'s squad for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">Euro 2012</a>, leading to strong speculation this was to avoid potential conflict with John Terry, who was included in the squad, due to Terry's upcoming trial for racially abusing Ferdinand's brother <a href="/wiki/Anton_Ferdinand" title="Anton Ferdinand">Anton</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Further controversy arose when after <a href="/wiki/Gary_Cahill" title="Gary Cahill">Gary Cahill</a> was ruled out of the tournament 22-year-old <a href="/wiki/Martin_Kelly" title="Martin Kelly">Martin Kelly</a> with just two minutes of international football was called up as a replacement instead of Ferdinand. This led to Ferdinand's representative Jamie Moralee accusing Hodgson of showing a "lack of respect".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 3 October 2012, the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mirror" title="Daily Mirror">Daily Mirror</a></i> reported that Roy Hodgson had revealed to fellow passengers on the <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a> that Ferdinand would no longer be considered for England duty, despite the retirement of John Terry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Hodgson later apologised for these comments and denied that he was ruling Ferdinand out of playing for England again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 March 2013, Ferdinand was recalled to the England squad for the first time under Hodgson for England's <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="2014 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">2014 World Cup qualifiers</a> against <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_national_football_team" title="San Marino national football team">San Marino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montenegro_national_football_team" title="Montenegro national football team">Montenegro</a>, though subsequently Ferdinand pulled out of the squad on 18 March due to 'fitness concerns'. Ferdinand said he was "gutted" at having to withdraw but said it was the "right decision". The England manager Roy Hodgson assured Ferdinand he still had an international future despite the withdrawal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2013, Ferdinand announced his retirement from international football, saying that "it's the right time to make room for young players and focus on the club career".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span></h2>
<p>Ferdinand was considered an atypical defensive product of English football due to his more elegant, "continental" style of defensive play;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mirror.co.uk_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-mirror.co.uk-79">[79]</a></sup> in particular, he was singled out for his unique technical ability and confidence on the ball, as well as his distribution and ability to play the ball on the ground.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent.co.uk_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-independent.co.uk-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bleacherreport.com_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-bleacherreport.com-82">[82]</a></sup> Ferdinand is regarded as one of the best defenders of his generation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> and as one of England's best ever centrebacks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mirror.co.uk_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-mirror.co.uk-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent.co.uk_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-independent.co.uk-81">[81]</a></sup> In his prime, he was also praised for his pace and tackling,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bleacherreport.com_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-bleacherreport.com-82">[82]</a></sup> in addition to his positioning and ability to read the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mirror.co.uk_79-2"><a href="#cite_note-mirror.co.uk-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> He was also a strong defender who was reliable in the air,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mirror.co.uk_79-3"><a href="#cite_note-mirror.co.uk-79">[79]</a></sup> with strong leadership qualities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bleacherreport.com_82-2"><a href="#cite_note-bleacherreport.com-82">[82]</a></sup></p>

<li><a href="/wiki/FIFPro#FIFA_FIFPro_World_XI" title="FIFPro">FIFPro World XI</a> (1): 2007–08<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/London_Youth_Games" title="London Youth Games">London Youth Games</a> Hall of Fame: 2010 inductee<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Premier_League_20_Seasons_Awards" title="Premier League 20 Seasons Awards">Premier League 20 Seasons Awards</a> (1992–93 to 2011–12)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup>

</li>

</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="FA_Commission">FA Commission</span></h2>
<p>On 20 October 2013, Ferdinand and <a href="/wiki/Roy_Hodgson" title="Roy Hodgson">Roy Hodgson</a> were appointed to the Football Association's commission to improve the state of the national game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Outside_football">Outside football</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rio_Ferdinand,_2004.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="358" data-file-width="257" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Rio_Ferdinand%2C_2004.jpg/170px-Rio_Ferdinand%2C_2004.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Rio_Ferdinand%2C_2004.jpg/255px-Rio_Ferdinand%2C_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/32/Rio_Ferdinand%2C_2004.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rio_Ferdinand,_2004.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ferdinand in 2004</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ferdinand grew up in the Friary council estate, <a href="/wiki/Peckham" title="Peckham">Peckham</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jones_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-Jones-13">[13]</a></sup> He has several brothers and sisters: one brother and three sisters on his father's side and a brother and sister from his mother's remarriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_10-5"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-10">[10]</a></sup> His brother, <a href="/wiki/Anton_Ferdinand" title="Anton Ferdinand">Anton Ferdinand</a>, is also a defender who now plays for League One club <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southend_United" title="Southend United">Southend United</a>, while former England striker <a href="/wiki/Les_Ferdinand" title="Les Ferdinand">Les Ferdinand</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Thurrock_United_F.C." title="East Thurrock United F.C.">East Thurrock United</a> midfielder <a href="/wiki/Kane_Ferdinand" title="Kane Ferdinand">Kane Ferdinand</a> are his cousins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jones_13-3"><a href="#cite_note-Jones-13">[13]</a></sup> Although he spent the majority of his career with Manchester United, he grew up supporting <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C.%E2%80%93Manchester_United_F.C._rivalry" title="Liverpool F.C.–Manchester United F.C. rivalry">rivals</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liverpool_FC" title="Liverpool FC">Liverpool</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006 in Manchester, Ferdinand's girlfriend Rebecca Ellison gave birth to their first son.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> The couple had two more children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> In 2010, Ferdinand <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ferdinand_v_Mirror_Group_Newspapers" title="Ferdinand v Mirror Group Newspapers">unsuccessfully sued</a> the <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Mirror" title="Sunday Mirror">Sunday Mirror</a></i> to prevent the publication of a story about an alleged affair with Carly Storey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> During the case, it was alleged that then-England captain Ferdinand had affairs with 10 different women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rebecca, who married Ferdinand in 2009, died of <a href="/wiki/Breast_cancer" title="Breast cancer">breast cancer</a> on 2 May 2015, aged 34.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ferdinand detailed his upbringing and outlook in his 2007 autobiography, <i>Rio: My Story</i>. Ferdinand is one of a small group of sportsmen to receive over £1 million as an advance for an autobiography. Ferdinand's experiences growing up in Peckham inspired him to set up the Rio Ferdinand Live the Dream Foundation in December 2009 to nurture and develop young people from deprived communities seeking careers in sports and entertainment. The foundation has received support from the UK Government and industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup> Ferdinand published his second volume of autobiography, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2Sides" title="2Sides">#2Sides</a></i> in 2014, following his career from beginning to his year at <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television.2C_film_and_music">Television, film and music</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Duran_Duran" title="Duran Duran">Duran Duran</a> song "<a href="/wiki/Rio_(song)" title="Rio (song)">Rio</a>" has been used in <a href="/wiki/Football_chant" title="Football chant">football chants</a> both for and against Ferdinand; in 2002, fan <a href="/wiki/Simon_Le_Bon" title="Simon Le Bon">Simon Le Bon</a> (Duran Duran's lead singer) promised to re-record one of the football chants if the team won.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ferdinand was sponsored by sportswear company <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a> and appeared in Nike commercials. In a global Nike advertising campaign in the run-up to the 2002 World Cup in Korea and Japan, he starred in a "<a href="/wiki/Secret_Tournament" title="Secret Tournament">Secret Tournament</a>" commercial (branded "Scopion KO") directed by <a href="/wiki/Terry_Gilliam" title="Terry Gilliam">Terry Gilliam</a>, appearing alongside football players such as <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Henry" title="Thierry Henry">Thierry Henry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronaldo_(Brazilian_footballer)" title="Ronaldo (Brazilian footballer)">Ronaldo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Totti" title="Francesco Totti">Francesco Totti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ronaldinho" title="Ronaldinho">Ronaldinho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Figo" title="Luís Figo">Luís Figo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fabio_Cannavaro" title="Fabio Cannavaro">Fabio Cannavaro</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hidetoshi_Nakata" title="Hidetoshi Nakata">Hidetoshi Nakata</a>, with former player <a href="/wiki/Eric_Cantona" title="Eric Cantona">Eric Cantona</a> the tournament "referee".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2005, Ferdinand, along with an old school friend, created the record label White Chalk Music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> To date, there are two artists signed to the label: Melody Johnston and Nia Jai. The latter released an album on 6 October 2010, which features Ferdinand rapping.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2006, on the day of the England national team's opening World Cup group match against <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_national_football_team" title="Paraguay national football team">Paraguay</a>, Ferdinand made his début appearance as a television presenter. Hosting <i><a href="/wiki/Rio%27s_World_Cup_Wind-Ups" title="Rio's World Cup Wind-Ups">Rio's World Cup Wind-Ups</a></i>, which was produced by his long-time business partner <a href="/wiki/Chris_Nathaniel" title="Chris Nathaniel">Chris Nathaniel</a> of <a href="/wiki/NVA_Entertainment" title="NVA Entertainment">NVA Entertainment</a>, the England defender found himself in a <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Beadle" title="Jeremy Beadle">Jeremy Beadle</a>-style role, playing tricks on his fellow England World Cup squad members including <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Rooney" title="Wayne Rooney">Wayne Rooney</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gary_Neville" title="Gary Neville">Gary Neville</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>He made his first foray into the world of cinema in late 2008, financing and becoming an executive producer of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alex_de_Rakoff" title="Alex de Rakoff">Alex de Rakoff</a>'s film <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dead_Man_Running_(film)" title="Dead Man Running (film)">Dead Man Running</a></i>. The film features <a href="/wiki/Danny_Dyer" title="Danny Dyer">Danny Dyer</a> and <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> in a gangster-themed plot. Ferdinand will share production credits with England team-mate <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Cole" title="Ashley Cole">Ashley Cole</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008. Ferdinand filmed a <a href="/wiki/Documentary_film" title="Documentary film">documentary</a> about Peckham, aiming to persuade youngsters away from a life of crime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 16 January 2009, it was announced that he would working with publishing company Made Up Media to launch a digital magazine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> In conjunction with this, Ferdinand was guest editor of the February edition of the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Observer_Sport_Monthly" title="Observer Sport Monthly">Observer Sport Monthly</a></i>, providing interviews with people ranging from <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Brown" title="Gordon Brown">Gordon Brown</a> to <a href="/wiki/Usain_Bolt" title="Usain Bolt">Usain Bolt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> The magazine, called "<a href="/wiki/5_Magazine" title="5 Magazine">#5 Magazine</a>", had its first issue published in April of that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span></h3>
<p>In 2000, Ferdinand briefly appeared in a sexually explicit video filmed at the <a href="/wiki/Ayia_Napa" title="Ayia Napa">Ayia Napa</a> resort in <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> along with fellow English footballers <a href="/wiki/Kieron_Dyer" title="Kieron Dyer">Kieron Dyer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lampard" title="Frank Lampard">Frank Lampard</a>. <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">Channel 4</a> aired a brief clip as part of their 2004 documentary <i>Sex, Footballers and Videotape</i>, claiming it was used to "remind the viewer that this is based on real life".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2002, during the rape trial of their acquaintance Martin King, Ferdinand and former Leeds colleague <a href="/wiki/Michael_Duberry" title="Michael Duberry">Michael Duberry</a> denied allegations that Duberry had molested the woman and Ferdinand had threatened her in the Leeds nightclub Hi-Fi on the night of 22 January, as well as further allegations of scuffling and drunkenness. Both men were interviewed by the police but the Crown Prosecution Service announced in April 2003 that they would not face charges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> King was found guilty of indecent assault and attempted rape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>During a radio interview on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chris_Moyles_Show" title="The Chris Moyles Show">The Chris Moyles Show</a></i> in October 2006, Ferdinand attracted two listener complaints and criticism from gay rights campaigner <a href="/wiki/Peter_Tatchell" title="Peter Tatchell">Peter Tatchell</a> when he called Moyles a <a href="/wiki/Faggot_(slang)" title="Faggot (slang)">faggot</a>, followed by "I'm sorry, I'm sorry, I'm sorry. I'm not <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homophobic" title="Homophobic">homophobic</a>", after Moyles had jokingly suggested he was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homosexual" title="Homosexual">homosexual</a>. <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">BBC Radio 1</a> later dismissed the exchange as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Banter" title="Banter">banter</a>, while Tatchell said "since [he] very promptly apologised, I am happy to accept his regret and leave it at that".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the wake of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R_v_John_Terry" title="R v John Terry">court case</a> involving <a href="/wiki/John_Terry" title="John Terry">John Terry</a> and Rio's brother <a href="/wiki/Anton_Ferdinand" title="Anton Ferdinand">Anton</a>, in which Terry was found not guilty of racial abuse, Rio Ferdinand sparked media controversy by expressing amusement at the comments of a <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> user who referred to <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Cole" title="Ashley Cole">Ashley Cole</a>, who had testified in Terry's favour, as a "choc ice", a slang term which is commonly understood to mean "<a href="/wiki/Uncle_Tom" title="Uncle Tom">black on the outside, white on the inside</a>". Ferdinand deleted the tweet shortly afterwards and denied <a href="/wiki/Choc_ice" title="Choc ice">choc ice</a> is a racist term, adding, "And if I want to laugh at something someone tweets....I will! Hahahahaha! Now stop getting ya knickers in a twist!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> Cole's lawyers released a statement in response, stating that he would not be taking the matter further.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> Ferdinand's words were condemned as "insensitive and untimely" by <a href="/wiki/Professional_Footballers%27_Association" title="Professional Footballers' Association">PFA</a> chief <a href="/wiki/Clarke_Carlisle" title="Clarke Carlisle">Clarke Carlisle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup> In August 2012, Ferdinand was fined £45,000 for his Twitter remarks after an Independent Regulatory Commission found him guilty of bringing the game into disrepute with an "improper" comment which included "a reference to ethnic origin, colour or race."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2014, Ferdinand was again charged by the FA for using offensive language on Twitter, after referring to the mother of a critic as a "sket", a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jamaican_slang" title="Jamaican slang">Jamaican slang</a> word for a promiscuous female.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> Ferdinand was fined £25,000 for the offence and banned from playing for three games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sketgate_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-sketgate-126">[125]</a></sup> The FA considered Ferdinand's position as a "role model" to be an aggravating factor for the penalty, in addition to it being his second Twitter offence within three years and no admission of wrongdoing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2015 it was announced that Ferdinand would be the new face of <a href="/wiki/Online_casino" title="Online casino">online casino</a> Casino Floor. The announcement provoked strong criticism on Twitter from a number of Ferdinand's followers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup> who suggested it was inappropriate that a role model for young people should endorse gambling particularly given the well documented struggles of many of his peers with <a href="/wiki/Problem_gambling" title="Problem gambling">problem gambling</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Driving_bans">Driving bans</span></h3>
<p>In September 1997, Ferdinand was convicted of <a href="/wiki/Driving_under_the_influence" title="Driving under the influence">drink-driving</a> and given a one-year driving ban. He had been breathalysed after driving on the morning after a night out, and was found to be one point over the limit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph24Nov2000DelBoy_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph24Nov2000DelBoy-129">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>As a result, England manager <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Hoddle" title="Glenn Hoddle">Glenn Hoddle</a> dropped Ferdinand from the squad to face Moldova in a <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="1998 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">World Cup qualification match</a> on 10 September, meaning Ferdinand lost out on the chance, at 18 years and 10 months of age, of becoming the youngest England international since <a href="/wiki/Duncan_Edwards" title="Duncan Edwards">Duncan Edwards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph24Nov2000DelBoy_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph24Nov2000DelBoy-129">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Independent3Sep1997Lesson_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Independent3Sep1997Lesson-130">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2003, Ferdinand was given another six-month ban from driving, and fined £2,500 and six penalty points for driving at an average of 92 mph (148 km/h) along the <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway" title="M1 motorway">M1</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> In May 2005, he was criticised by a <a href="/wiki/Magistrate" title="Magistrate">magistrate</a> as he received his fourth ban from driving and a fine of £1,500, after being caught by traffic police "travelling at an average of 105.9 mph (170.4 km/h) over a distance of nearly two miles" on the <a href="/wiki/M6_motorway" title="M6 motorway">M6 motorway</a>. Upon setting the penalty, the magistrate said Ferdinand "should be a positive role model for young people in society and this does not give out the right message". It followed two previous bans for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Speeding" title="Speeding">speeding</a>, in 2002 and 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2012 Ferdinand was given a six-month ban from driving after being caught speeding three times in six weeks on the same road. Ferdinand already had three points on his licence after twice being caught speeding in the same area in January.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> Nine days after this ban ended, Ferdinand was fined £200 and received three penalty points after being caught speeding along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A34_road_(England)" title="A34 road (England)">A34</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup></p>
